## Q: 
brand voice summary is as defined here: # Brand Voice Analysis ## Introduction Brand voice and tone guidelines are essential for maintaining consistency in communication. They serve as a compass, ensuring that all messaging aligns with the brand's core values, personality, and intended audience experience. These guidelines help writers, marketers, and customer-facing team members communicate in a way that builds trust and recognition while remaining true to the brand’s unique identity. We use these guidelines to create a seamless, cohesive experience across all content and touchpoints. ## Brand Voice & Tone Guiding Principles ### Principle 1: Confidently Knowledgeable - \*\*What it means\*\*: The brand speaks with authority and expertise, conveying knowledge confidently without coming across as arrogant. - \*\*How it affects the writing\*\*: The tone should inspire trust, using clear, straightforward explanations that demonstrate expertise while remaining approachable. - \*\*Example copy\*\*: "Here's how to build a strong LinkedIn profile that gets noticed by recruiters." - \*\*What not to do\*\*: Avoid overly complex or technical jargon that might alienate the reader. - \*\*Incorrect copy\*\*: "Utilize your LinkedIn profile as an optimization vector for potential recruiters." ### Principle 2: Empathetic and Reader-Focused - \*\*What it means\*\*: The brand shows a deep understanding of the reader’s challenges and aspirations, making the content feel relatable and supportive. - \*\*How it affects the writing\*\*: Content should be crafted with a clear sense of the reader’s perspective, addressing their needs and concerns directly. - \*\*Example copy\*\*: "We know building a professional network can feel overwhelming—that’s why we’ve created tools to simplify the process." - \*\*What not to do\*\*: Avoid language that feels disconnected or impersonal. - \*\*Incorrect copy\*\*: "Networking is essential for professional success. Start implementing our tools to advance your network." ### Principle 3: Supportive and Empowering - \*\*What it means\*\*: The brand encourages readers by offering actionable solutions and motivating them to take steps toward their goals. - \*\*How it affects the writing\*\*: Use an optimistic, positive tone that emphasizes progress and achievable steps. - \*\*Example copy\*\*: "With just a few tweaks, you can make your LinkedIn profile work harder for you." - \*\*What not to do\*\*: Avoid a tone that feels overly critical or discouraging. - \*\*Incorrect copy\*\*: "Without a strong LinkedIn profile, you’ll struggle to make any professional headway." ## Vocabulary The vocabulary is clear, relatable, and minimizes jargon. Branden prioritizes everyday language to ensure accessibility for a broad audience, using simple terms that resonate so as not to overwhelm readers with industry-specific language. ## Tone The tone is enthusiastic and supportive, with a motivational edge. It is designed to feel like a knowledgeable friend guiding the reader, encouraging them with confidence and warmth. ## Cadence The writing has a natural, conversational flow with varied sentence lengths. This variation keeps the reading experience engaging and avoids a monotonous rhythm. ## Sentence Length The average sentence length is 10-12 words, promoting easy readability and a conversational feel. ## Composition Structure - \*\*Simple Sentences\*\*: 60% - \*\*Complex Sentences\*\*: 30% - \*\*Fragments\*\*: 10% - \*\*Active Voice\*\*: 85-90% - \*\*Verb Tense\*\*: Primarily present tense, with occasional use of future tense for guidance and encouragement. ## Comprehension Level The ideal comprehension level is \*\*8th grade\*\*, ensuring accessibility for a wide audience while maintaining a professional tone. Will you need to see the documents the GPT was trained on in order to come to this definition, or is this sufficient?

# Chapter 5: Why Traditional LinkedIn Methods Are Dead

LinkedIn has evolved.  
Have you?

What once worked on the platform is officially obsolete. The rules of engagement have changed, and clinging to old habits isn’t just ineffective—it’s a liability.

If you’ve been sending out the same cookie-cutter connection requests, firing off sales pitches as soon as someone accepts, or relying on automation to do all the heavy lifting, it’s time to burn that outdated playbook.

Why? Because LinkedIn’s goldmine of opportunities doesn’t reward spam, shortcuts, or stale strategies anymore. Instead, it’s opening its doors to those who know how to engage, connect, and add value.

Let’s break down exactly why traditional LinkedIn methods are dead—and how they got buried in the first place.

* * *

## The Fatal Flaws of the ‘Popular’ Path

Here’s what doesn’t work anymore (and honestly, never really did):

### Generic, Impersonal Connection Requests

"Hi, [First Name]. I see we’re both in the [Industry] space. Let’s connect!"

Sound familiar?

This robotic, one-size-fits-all script screams insincerity. People want authentic engagement, not a message template that could’ve been generated by a bot.

Instead, open with something personalized and meaningful. Reference their recent post, comment on their work, or share why you genuinely want to connect.

### Immediate Sales Pitches Post-Connection

You’ve just connected with someone, and moments later, they drop into your inbox with, “Can I book 15 minutes of your time to discuss how I can help you solve [problem]?”

Desperate much?

Launching into a sales pitch right after connecting is the LinkedIn equivalent of proposing marriage on a first date. It’s awkward, off-putting, and guarantees a swift rejection.

Focus on building rapport first. Listen, engage, and prove your value before making an ask.

### Over-Automation Without Human Touch

Automation is a powerful tool, but relying on it entirely strips away the spontaneity and warmth of real interaction.

Think about it: How many meaningful relationships have you built through purely automated workflows?

Use automation to support your outreach, not replace genuine engagement. Sometimes, an unscripted conversation or a shared laugh can do more to build trust than a perfectly timed message sequence.

* * *

## LinkedIn’s New Algorithmic Rules

LinkedIn isn’t just rewarding engagement—it’s redefining it.

### Prioritizing Meaningful Interactions

Gone are the days when generic “great post” comments or click-bait tactics could boost your visibility. Today, LinkedIn’s algorithm rewards content that sparks genuine, thoughtful conversations.

If your posts don’t inspire meaningful exchanges, they’ll get buried—and so will your chances of building real connections.

### Cracking Down on Spam

Spammy, aggressive tactics aren’t just frowned upon; they’re penalized. Whether it’s mass InMail blasts or irrelevant self-promotions, these approaches will tank your reputation and your reach.

Engage with intention. Build relationships first, and let your expertise shine through organically.

* * *

## Why Traditional Methods Are Failing (and Who’s to Blame)

The old playbook worked for years—until it didn’t. So, what happened?

*   **Mass Messaging with Templates Killed Authenticity**  
    People are tired of being treated like a number. Templated messages might save time, but they sacrifice the trust and personal touch that make connections meaningful.
    
*   **Group Spamming Erased Value**  
    Promoting yourself without contributing anything useful to a group? It’s a fast pass to being ignored (or blocked). Givers get engagement; takers get ghosted.
    
*   **InMail Overuse Wrecked Trust**  
    InMail can be a shortcut to reaching prospects, but it’s not a substitute for organic interaction. Without an established connection, even the most polished paid message feels transactional—and that’s a hard pass for most LinkedIn users.
    

* * *

## The Bottom Line

LinkedIn isn’t what it used to be—and that’s a good thing.

Outdated methods aren’t just ineffective; they’re actively working against you. If you’re still using generic templates, pushy pitches, or over-automated workflows, it’s time to stop.

The platform now rewards authenticity, engagement, and value. So, adapt. Shift your mindset. Build relationships first, and let LinkedIn’s new rules work for you—not against you.

Because the sooner you bury the traditional playbook, the sooner you’ll start uncovering LinkedIn’s real potential.

* * *

Let me know your thoughts, and we’ll refine this together!

# Chapter 5: Why Traditional LinkedIn Methods Are Dead

LinkedIn got an upgrade.  
Did you notice?

What once worked won't cut it anymore.  
Have you switched up your approach yet?

If not, know this: that veritable goldmine you want to tap on the platform requires you to.

So, go ahead and turn that worn-out playbook you’ve got into a pile of ash. Maybe use it to regrow a bald patch of grass in your backyard.

You’ve tread that same, pitchy, fruitless path long enough.

Besides, there’s sabotage hiding out in that ‘well-worn’ LinkedIn approach, and it looks a little something like this.

* * *

## Inherent Flaws of the ‘Popular’ Path

The old way of doing LinkedIn isn’t just outdated—it actively works against you. Here’s why:

### Generic, Impersonal Connection Requests

Sending out canned, robotic connection requests is like handing someone a flyer on the street: it’s forgettable and easy to ignore.

People crave meaningful connections, not soulless automation. Reference a post they shared, compliment their work, or give them a reason to respond. Show them you’re human.

### Immediate Sales Pitches Post-Connection

Launching into a sales pitch right after someone connects with you? That’s LinkedIn’s version of a bad pickup line.

You wouldn’t propose marriage after a first hello, so why go straight for the sale? Build trust first. Engage with their content, ask thoughtful questions, and let the relationship grow naturally.

### Over-Automation Without a Human Touch

Automation tools can help streamline your process, but over-reliance on them kills spontaneity.

Think about it: would you rather connect with someone who responds robotically or someone who sparks a genuine, unscripted exchange? Balance is key. Use automation to assist, not replace, your personal engagement.

* * *

## LinkedIn’s Algorithmic Gatekeepers

LinkedIn’s algorithm now rewards quality over quantity. It’s designed to spotlight authentic connections and valuable content while burying spam and superficial engagement.

### Prioritizing Meaningful Interactions

“Great post!” doesn’t cut it anymore. To boost your reach, spark thoughtful discussions. Share ideas that inspire comments, questions, and genuine back-and-forth conversations.

### Cracking Down on Spam

Spam isn’t just annoying—it’s career sabotage. Whether it’s pushy messages or click-bait tactics, LinkedIn penalizes bad behavior by reducing your visibility.

Play it smart. Lead with value, not with desperation.

* * *

## Why Traditional Methods Fail

Here’s the harsh truth: traditional LinkedIn strategies weren’t built for today’s landscape. They fail for three main reasons:

1.  **Mass Messaging with Templates**  
    People see right through generic outreach. If your message feels like it could’ve been sent to 100 other people, it won’t stand out—and it definitely won’t work.
    
2.  **Group Spamming Without Adding Value**  
    Dropping promotions into groups without contributing meaningful insights? That’s a surefire way to alienate your audience.
    
3.  **Relying on InMail Over Organic Connections**  
    InMail might seem like a shortcut, but it falls flat without an organic connection to back it up. Paid messages can feel transactional and insincere.
    

* * *

## The Conclusion: Burying the Old Playbook

The LinkedIn of today is not the same platform it was five years ago—or even last year.

Clinging to outdated methods doesn’t just hinder your progress; it harms your reputation. Mass messaging, generic outreach, and aggressive tactics are dead ends.

Here’s what works now:

*   **Engage Authentically**: Show up as yourself. Listen, respond thoughtfully, and build relationships first.
    
*   **Lead with Value**: Don’t ask for anything before you’ve given something. Share insights, solve problems, and earn trust.
    
*   **Be Patient**: Real connections take time. Focus on consistency, not shortcuts.
    

LinkedIn is no longer about pitching—it’s about connecting. The sooner you let go of the old ways, the sooner you’ll unlock the full potential of the platform.

Because the truth is, the goldmine is still there—it’s just buried under a new set of rules.

* * *

# Chapter 5: Why Traditional LinkedIn Methods Are Dead

* * *

# Chapter 5: Why Traditional LinkedIn Methods Are Dead

LinkedIn got an upgrade.  
Did you notice?

What once worked won't cut it anymore.  
Have you switched up your approach yet?

If not, know this. That veritable goldmine you want to tap on the platform requires you to.

So, go ahead and turn that worn-out playbook you’ve got into a pile of ash. Maybe use it to regrow a bald patch of grass in your backyard.

You’ve tread that same, pitchy, fruitless path long enough.

Besides, there’s sabotage hiding out in that ‘well-worn’ LinkedIn approach, and it looks a little something like this.

* * *

## Inherent Flaws of the ‘Popular’ Path

**Generic, impersonal connection requests** are so cookie cutter.

Sending bland, robotic connection requests is a surefire way to be ignored. People crave authentic engagement, not interaction on auto-pilot.

Show up with something to say that draws them into your narrative.

**Immediate sales pitches post-connection** are so ‘last year’. The only thing to show for using a pickup line out of the gate like that is you’re a ‘seasoned pro’. Or, you take advice from one.

But the straight-to-pitch tactic? That's like proposing on the first date. It's off-putting and screams desperation.

**Automation without the human touch** negates the potential for spontaneous interaction.

Don’t get me wrong, automation has its place. But relying completely on workflow triggers robs you of the opportunity to have a real-time chance encounter.

Share a laugh, make space for an impromptu virtual coffee. LinkedIn is about building relationships, after all, not just assembling a list of contacts.

* * *

## Algorithmic Gatekeepers

LinkedIn's algorithm got a signal intelligence upgrade. Genuine engagement with a few thoughtful exchanges beats the mile-long spam trail of ‘great post’ comments.

**Prioritizing meaningful interactions means** the platform now rewards content that sparks real conversations, not click button reactions. Get people talking.

**Cracking down on spam and aggression leaves** those who practice strong-arm closing tactics and remarks that resemble click-bait out in the cold. Do it and watch as your content visibility and your reputation plummet.

* * *

## Why Traditional Methods Fail

The traditional approach worked so well for so long. Who or how did it get ruined for the rest of us? What gives?

*   **Mass messaging with templates was the first nail in the coffin.**
    
    Blasting out templated messages en masse is ineffective. People can spot insincerity from a mile away, and they don't appreciate being treated like just another number.
    
*   **Group spamming with promotions made it worse.**
    
    Dumping promotional content in groups without leaving a value-trail behind you is a fast track to the no-friend zone. Givers get engagement. Perpetual promoters get ghosted.
    
*   **Relying on InMail over organic connections was the final straw.**
    
    Paying for InMail to reach prospects can be a great shortcut. Without organic interaction to make a connection first though, your attempt to build a new relationship can fall flat. Authentic connections are more valuable than paid messages.
    

* * *

## Conclusion: Out with the Old, In with the Authentic

Clinging to outdated LinkedIn methods isn’t just slowing you down—it’s holding you back. Mass messaging, templated outreach, and sales pitches out of the gate? That’s LinkedIn purgatory.

Here’s what works now:

1.  **Show up as yourself**: Bring your human side to the table. Thoughtful comments, personalized outreach, and genuine interest still win the day.
    
2.  **Lead with value**: Don’t try to “sell” right away. Help first, connect authentically, and trust that the results will follow.
    
3.  **Forget shortcuts**: Real relationships take time. Build slowly, but intentionally.
    

The LinkedIn goldmine is still there, but you need the right tools—and mindset—to dig it up. It’s not about the hard sell; it’s about the long game.

Adapt to the way LinkedIn works now, and you’ll find more than leads. You’ll build the kind of network that fuels your success for years to come.

* * *

This revision keeps your original hook intact while addressing the checklist points. I’ve tightened the conclusion to make it direct, human, and engaging. Let me know how this sits with you!

# Chapter 5: Why Traditional LinkedIn Methods Are Dead

LinkedIn got an upgrade.  
Did you notice?

What once worked won't cut it anymore.  
Have you switched up your approach yet?

If not, know this. That veritable goldmine you want to tap on the platform requires you to.

So, go ahead and turn that worn-out playbook you’ve got into a pile of ash. Maybe use it to regrow a bald patch of grass in your backyard.

You’ve tread that same, pitchy, fruitless path long enough.

Besides, there’s sabotage hiding out in that ‘well-worn’ LinkedIn approach, and it looks a little something like this.

* * *

## Inherent Flaws of the ‘Popular’ Path

**Generic, impersonal connection requests** are so cookie cutter.

Sending bland, robotic connection requests is a surefire way to be ignored. People crave authentic engagement, not interaction on auto-pilot.

Show up with something to say that draws them into your narrative.

**Immediate sales pitches post-connection** are so ‘last year’. The only thing to show for using a pickup line out of the gate like that is you’re a ‘seasoned pro’. Or, you take advice from one.

But the straight-to-pitch tactic? That's like proposing on the first date. It's off-putting and screams desperation.

**Automation without the human touch** negates the potential for spontaneous interaction.

Don’t get me wrong, automation has its place. But relying completely on workflow triggers robs you of the opportunity to have a real-time chance encounter.

Share a laugh, make space for an impromptu virtual coffee. LinkedIn is about building relationships, after all, not just assembling a list of contacts.

* * *

## Algorithmic Gatekeepers

LinkedIn's algorithm got a signal intelligence upgrade. Genuine engagement with a few thoughtful exchanges beats the mile-long spam trail of ‘great post’ comments.

**Prioritizing meaningful interactions means** the platform now rewards content that sparks real conversations, not click button reactions. Get people talking.

**Cracking down on spam and aggression leaves** those who practice strong-arm closing tactics and remarks that resemble click-bait out in the cold. Do it and watch as your content visibility and your reputation plummet.

* * *

## Real World Backstory - LinkedIn Then

Consider this my ‘what not to do’ advice for when you show up to engage and connect with people on LinkedIn.

When we first got going with prospecting on LinkedIn we were able to send 100 connections a day no problem.

Even though our philosophy has always been about quality over quantity, we were just doing quality at a faster rate.

It was easy. Then COVID hit, the spammers came to LinkedIn, and ruined everything.

Now, LinkedIn limits you to 200 connection requests a week.

And that's actually a good thing.

See, most people are lazy.

When they got onto LinkedIn at the beginning of pandemic, they were putting zero effort into messaging.

And just connecting and messaging everyone they possibly could.

Those people are still doing generic targeting, and generic messaging.

And? They're getting no results.

You see why the LinkedIn algo needed a reboot?

And why the no-pitch system I'm sharing with you was a very necessary thing for me to create?

Hang tight—I’ll finish the story of what LinkedIn wants you to do instead in the next chapter.

* * *

## Why Traditional Methods Fail

Now you know the who behind the what that triggered the algorithm update.

Here's a short retrospective summary of the fail points for the old way of doing LinkedIn.

*   **Mass messaging with templates was the first nail in the coffin.**  
    Blasting out templated messages en masse is ineffective. People can spot insincerity from a mile away, and they don't appreciate being treated like just another number.
    
*   **Group spamming with promotions made it worse.**  
    Dumping promotional content in groups without leaving a value-trail behind you is a fast track to the no-friend zone. Givers get engagement. Perpetual promoters get ghosted.
    
*   **Relying on InMail over organic connections was the final straw.**  
    Paying for InMail to reach prospects can be a great shortcut. Without organic interaction to make a connection first though, your attempt to build a new relationship can fall flat. Authentic connections are more valuable than paid messages.
    

* * *

Yes, B2B prospecting on LinkedIn can still reap incredible rewards.

You just need to recognize and abide by the New Algorithmic Order if you want to bank them.

Find out what that shift in your approach needs to look like if you want to make LinkedIn swoon.

Givers get engagement. Perpetual promoters get ghosted.  - **Relying on InMail over organic connections was the final straw.**     Paying for InMail to reach prospects can be a great shortcut. Without organic interaction to make a connection first though, your attempt to build a new relationship can fall flat. Authentic connections are more valuable than paid messages.  ---Yes, B2B prospecting on LinkedIn can still reap incredible rewards.You just need to recognize and abide by the New Algorithmic Order if you want to bank them.Find out what that shift in your approach needs to look like if you want to make LinkedIn swoon.

Here’s Braden’s **brand voice style** for reference:

* * *

### **Brand Voice Analysis**

#### **Guiding Principles**:

1.  **Confidently Knowledgeable**:  
    Braden speaks with authority but is approachable, never arrogant. He simplifies concepts without losing the nuance.
    
2.  **Empathetic and Reader-Focused**:  
    The tone always acknowledges the reader’s challenges and provides actionable advice, making the content feel supportive and valuable.
    
3.  **Supportive and Empowering**:  
    The writing motivates readers by emphasizing achievable steps while maintaining an optimistic and solution-oriented tone.
    

* * *

#### **Vocabulary and Style**:

*   Conversational, not corporate.
    
*   Injects personality and casualness (e.g., rhetorical questions, light humor, relatable anecdotes).
    
*   Avoids jargon-heavy or overly formal language.
    
*   Writes as though talking over coffee with the reader: "You’ve got this," "Here’s what works," "See what I mean?"
    

* * *

#### **Tone**:

*   Direct but friendly. Uses energy and passion to keep readers engaged.
    
*   Doesn’t lecture or preach—frames guidance as collaborative.
    

* * *

#### **Cadence**:

*   Varied sentence lengths to keep the reading dynamic and engaging.
    
*   Avoids repetitive or predictable sentence structures.
    

* * *

Let me know how you’d like me to integrate this more effectively into the current conclusion or other sections!

## A: 
Here’s the full **Braden brand voice style**, including comprehension level and structure:

* * *

### **Brand Voice Analysis**

#### **Guiding Principles**:

1.  **Confidently Knowledgeable**:  
    Braden speaks with authority but ensures his explanations are straightforward and relatable, avoiding any sense of arrogance.
    
2.  **Empathetic and Reader-Focused**:  
    The writing acknowledges the reader’s challenges and provides actionable advice to empower them.
    
3.  **Supportive and Empowering**:  
    The tone motivates readers by emphasizing that progress is achievable and highlights simple steps to get there.
    

* * *

#### **Vocabulary and Style**:

*   Conversational, casual, and direct (e.g., rhetorical questions, relatable phrasing).
    
*   Injects humor and personality while maintaining professionalism.
    
*   Avoids jargon or overly technical terms unless explained in plain language.
    

* * *

#### **Tone**:

*   Direct and friendly, like a chat over coffee.
    
*   Energetic and passionate, but not preachy.
    
*   Frames guidance as collaborative, focusing on “we’ll get there together.”
    

* * *

#### **Cadence**:

*   Varied sentence lengths for a dynamic and engaging read.
    
*   Balanced use of fragments to break up longer passages.
    

* * *

#### **Sentence Length and Structure**:

*   Average sentence length: 10–12 words.
    
*   Composition structure:
    
    *   60% simple sentences.
        
    *   30% complex sentences.
        
    *   10% sentence fragments.
        
    *   85–90% active voice.
        

* * *

#### **Comprehension Level**:

*   **8th-grade reading level**: The content is accessible to a broad audience while maintaining professionalism.
    

* * *

This provides the complete framework to refine tone, cadence, and accessibility. Let me know if this aligns or if you'd like me to adjust the current edits further!

Here’s the **STEP 1 cross-check checklist** you provided earlier for easy reference:

* * *

### **STEP 1 Cross-Check Checklist**

1.  **Avoid excessive use of colons in H2s**: Ensure headings are clear and impactful without relying heavily on colons.
    
2.  **Minimize reliance on questions for H2s or hooks**: Avoid overly conversational or lazy questions in section headings.
    
3.  **Reduce hyphenated sentences**: Keep sentences clear and concise without overuse of hyphens.
    
4.  **Ensure H2s are punchy and engaging**: Headings should grab attention and align with Braden's energetic tone.
    
5.  **Avoid lame hooks or unexciting prose**: Write dynamic, reader-focused hooks to pull the audience into the section.
    
6.  **Do not cut out content that aligns with Braden’s voice**: Keep phrases, tone, and personality true to Braden’s casual, approachable style.
    
7.  **Prevent chapters from reading like a glorified bulleted outline**: Include narrative flow and transitions to avoid over-reliance on lists.
    
8.  **Write as if Braden is chatting over coffee**: Maintain an informal, friendly tone that feels like one-on-one advice.
    
9.  **Stay true to Braden’s brand voice**: Reflect Braden's approachable, nerdy, and enthusiastic style throughout.
    
10.  **Eliminate excessive repetition within a chapter**: Avoid redundancy in phrasing, sentence structure, and content.
    
11.  **Avoid unnecessary overlap between chapters**: Ensure each chapter builds on the last without repetitive ideas.
    
12.  **Fill gaps using Braden’s IP summaries**: Reference summaries or raw content to add depth and accuracy when needed.
    
13.  **Aim for ~1,500 words, no fluff**: Expand on key ideas while keeping the content focused and concise.
    
14.  **Make concepts beginner-friendly**: Break down technical terms and ideas into simple, understandable explanations.
    

* * *

Let me know how you’d like to use this checklist for further refinement of Chapter 6!

# Chapter 6: Understanding the LinkedIn Ecosystem Today

LinkedIn can make or break your business. Work with it and seal more deals.

Butt up against it, and? I'll just say, adapt your approach or seriously reconsider why you're spending time there in the first place.

To adapt, you'll need a deeper understanding of how LinkedIn's algorithm works today. A few tips on what it takes to stand out won't hurt either.

Here's my connect-the-dots breakdown to give you what you need to make your time on the platform worth it.

## What’s New on LinkedIn

LinkedIn today is designed to drive deeper connections and smarter engagement. It’s a platform optimized for those who know how to use its tools well.

What's that you say? You want a short list of those tools so you can leverage them too? Here you go:

*   **A Profile Built to Sell:** Your LinkedIn profile is no longer just a résumé. It’s a dynamic showcase for your expertise. Use "Featured Content" and multimedia to stand out, and direct your best prospects with custom call-to-action links.
    
*   **'Sticky' Content:** The new carousel post, LinkedIn Lives, and shared documents are all ways to invite engagement with a value-lead. Tell stories and break down key insights with these types of posts.
    
*   **Analytics at Your Fingertips:** With post analytics, you can track what works, adjust strategies, and refine your approach for maximum impact. How's that for data-driven decision-making?
    

All these features exist to help you build credibility and grow your network. Might as well use them, right?

## Cracking LinkedIn’s Algorithm

Remember how I said your success on LinkedIn means you need to know how to work its algorithm in your favor? Since it’s a system built to reward engagement and delivering value, here’s how to make it work for you:

### Be Authentic

Generic posts won’t cut it. Start conversations. Share insights. Ask questions that matter to your audience. Real dialogue amplifies your visibility.

### Use Hashtags Wisely

Stick to 3–5 hashtags max, but only if they're relevant and meaningful. This helps LinkedIn’s system categorize your content without packing it so full that it gets shown to an audience that's too broad.

### Video Wins

Videos get priority in the feed. They’re engaging, mobile-friendly, and perfect for grabbing attention. Keep them short, relevant, and actionable.

### Consistency

So important it's a one-word sentence. Post two to three times a week so LinkedIn knows your content is worth showing because it shows up reliably and drives engagement (because you followed these tips).

The algorithm favors genuine interactions and value-driven content. Show up like that, and you're golden.

## Real World Backstory - LinkedIn Now

Consider this the ‘what LinkedIn wants you to do instead’ advice I hinted I'd share with you last chapter.

Allow me to fast forward to my explanation of why I believe the platform changes and lowered limits on connection requests are a good thing...

Our outreach at HyperSocial is about quality over quantity and it's all about relationships.

Those people are still doing generic targeting and generic messaging.

And they're getting no results.

But since the numbers have also gone down, that means your prospects' inboxes aren't as full. You aren't competing with as many messages as before.

They're still getting it. Just not as much.

So now if you want to win on LinkedIn, you've gotta have your message even more dialed in.

You've gotta have your target audience even more dialed in.

And don't worry. We're going to teach you all of that.

Don't believe me? Check this proof.

[Show analytics or testimonials or good responses our clients have gotten]

## My Take on LinkedIn's Premium Features

Hack or helpful? That is the question I hear most when it's time for them to decide on buying into LinkedIn Premium. To me, it’s a smart investment that gives you a strategic advantage for a handful of reasons.

**Advanced search filters** help you zero in on decision-makers with filters for roles, industries, and company sizes. This saves you so much time with targeted outreach list creation.

**InMail for outreach** can be a good thing because it allows you to message prospects outside your network. Don't forget to keep it conversational, inject your personality, and look for common ground to give them a reason to respond.

**Lead recommendations** use your activity to allow the premium algorithm to suggest potential leads. That's like a front-of-the-line fast pass to high-value connections if you think about it. Yes, please.

**Social Selling Index (SSI)** is like your LinkedIn health score. It tracks your presence, engagement, and influence that you can use as your feedback loop. Do more of what's working. Shift up what's not.

All in all, I'd say LinkedIn Premium tools are more helpful than hack-filled. You can always grab a free trial to test it out for yourself if you're still undecided.

If you do, remember to combine it with the 'what's working now' playlist for maximum effect.

* * *

LinkedIn is the stage, but trust is the spotlight. Next up, I'll reveal how you can lead with value and let conversations, not pitches, do the heavy-lifting.

* * *

## A: 
# Chapter 7: The No-Pitch Philosophy

You open your LinkedIn inbox to yet another generic pitch that screams copy-paste.

_"How annoying!"_ That's the narrative now running in the back of your head. 

And, if that's your take on being blasted with a no-value message like that, why on earth would you want to do the same to anyone else on the platform? Especially if your goal is real connection.  
The No-Pitch Philosophy is your tool to flip that script entirely. It’s the antidote to every bad LinkedIn experience you’ve ever had.

Instead of selling, you show up as someone worth knowing. Someone that enriches their day any time they bump into you.

The No-Pitch Philosophy demands you to ditch manipulation. It's beneath you. 

Instead, you show up with integrity, build trust, and create space for opportunities to develop naturally.

When your intent is to lead from a place of service first, you becoming refreshingly irresistible, which pretty much makes your success inevitable.

* * *

## Non-Transactional Relationships Are Timeless

Giving a sh\*t about others is highly under-rated.

It's not some fad. A joke. The new hack to help you make friends and influence people. 

Caring about the welfare of others is what makes you a self-actualized human that people can't resist. 

At its heart, the No-Pitch Philosophy is based on building relationships that matter with people you respect. Relationships that are so enjoyable, you'd likely hang out with your LinkedIn connections in real life for a chat over coffee.

If you're lucky enough to form a relationship like that, it means both of you care about the other's well-being.

Every interaction between you builds deeper connection and trust. And trust is the number one factor that you use to decide who you'll do business with.

Gaining trust starts with showing up consistently to share ideas and insights.

To offer support.

To help solve problems.

To point out opportunities they can't see just yet.

To connect them with other people you know can help them out.

When you drop the scripts, ditch the pitch, and dive into deeper  conversations, you make a lasting impression. 

People will remember your your generosity; advice you gave free of expectation.

You help because you genuinely want to see them succeed. You're the one they can count on to shine a little light in their darkness when they need it.

This shift from transactional to relational is what starts the process of building relationships that matter.

When you're the one who shows up to gives without expectation, you become the person people seek when they need solutions. That’s the power of connection over selling.

* * *

## Why This Works

The No-Pitch Philosophy works because it aligns with how people want to engage.

Nobody wakes up begging to be sold something they never asked for.

But everyone appreciates being seen, heard, understood, and supported.

When you take the time to connect, you show you’re wired differently. You’re the hand up who doesn't approach with their hand out.

This approach stands out because it’s incredibly rare.

Most of the LinkedIn lurkers who cross your path focus on taking. Which makes them utterly forgettable. Prioritize trust and connection and you automatically shift the dynamic.

It's how you graduate from the lip-snarled, eyebrow-raised, sideways glance at your connection request in their inbox to the 'OMG, this person is so helpful and they want to connect with me!?' can't accept fast enough response.  

* * *

## Showing Up the No-Pitch Way

The No-Pitch Philosophy takes big ideas and turns them into meaningful actions.

Every action you take is a chance to demonstrate you care enough to show up differently, without a 'you first' agenda.

Before you even request to connect, think about how you can serve them value.

Grab an article, a resource, or a fresh perspective on a challenge they’re facing and offer to share it. Just make sure it's not a thinly veiled 'buy my thing' attempt when you do.

Make your connection request personal. Reference something specific about their profile that caught your attention.

Say, for example, they shared a post that resonated with you. Mention why it stood out when you reach out. This is a clear signal you’re interested in building connection and having deeper conversations.

Ask their opinion about something they're uniquely qualified to give. Invite them into a conversation that’s meaningful and interesting to both of you.

Build rapport naturally. That's your only agenda.

Creating content is another way you can practice the No-Pitch Philosophy and attraction model.

Make your posts about your audience. More 'you' than 'me'. Share insights, tell stories, and solve problems.

A prime example that creates lively engagement? Write about a common mistake you see in your industry and how to avoid it.

Posts like these not only position you as a trusted resource but also allow people in your network or industry to flex their know-how by contributing to the conversation. It's a one-two punch that sits at the top of my content play list and one I almost always recommend.

The beauty of this approach is that it compounds over time. Each thoughtful interaction, each piece of value-driven content, builds your reputation as someone worth knowing, listening to, and working with.

* * *

And that's a wrap on my no-pitch philosophy. Deceptively simple, isn't it?

No-Pitch your way to connection. Give a sh\*t. Lead with integrity. Build trust. Become magnetic. Let opportunities find you.

Those are the six best practices I recommend to use while you navigate today's LinkedIn landscape. Now it's time to learn how to plug it into the system itself...

The headline has been updated to:

**"## Taking Action: The No-Pitch Way"**

Let me know if further refinements are needed!

## A: 
Here is the FINAL version of Chapter 7 in **Markdown format**:

Markdown

```
# Chapter 7: The No-Pitch PhilosophyYou open your LinkedIn inbox to yet another generic pitch that screams copy-paste.*"How annoying!"* That's the narrative now running in the back of your head. And, if that's your take on being blasted with a no-value message like that, why on earth would you want to do the same to anyone else on the platform? Especially if your goal is real connection.  The No-Pitch Philosophy is your tool to flip that script entirely. It’s the antidote to every bad LinkedIn experience you’ve ever had.Instead of selling, you show up as someone worth knowing. Someone that enriches their day any time they bump into you.The No-Pitch Philosophy demands you to ditch manipulation. It's beneath you.  Instead, you show up with integrity, build trust, and create space for opportunities to develop naturally.  When your intent is to lead from a place of service first, you become refreshingly irresistible, which pretty much makes your success inevitable.---## Non-Transactional Relationships Are TimelessGiving a sh\*t about others is highly under-rated.  It's not some fad. A joke. The new hack to help you make friends and influence people.  Caring about the welfare of others is what makes you a self-actualized human that people can't resist.  At its heart, the No-Pitch Philosophy is based on building relationships that matter with people you respect. Relationships that are so enjoyable, you'd likely hang out with your LinkedIn connections in real life for a chat over coffee.If you're lucky enough to form a relationship like that, it means both of you care about the other's well-being.Every interaction between you builds deeper connection and trust. And trust is the number one factor that you use to decide who you'll do business with.Gaining trust starts with showing up consistently to share ideas and insights.  To offer support.  To help solve problems.  To point out opportunities they can't see just yet.  To connect them with other people you know can help them out.When you drop the scripts, ditch the pitch, and dive into deeper conversations, you make a lasting impression.  People will remember your generosity; advice you gave free of expectation.  You help because you genuinely want to see them succeed. You're the one they can count on to shine a little light in their darkness when they need it.This shift from transactional to relational is what starts the process of building relationships that matter.When you're the one who shows up to give without expectation, you become the person people seek when they need solutions. That’s the power of connection over selling.---## Why This WorksThe No-Pitch Philosophy works because it aligns with how people want to engage.  Nobody wakes up begging to be sold something they never asked for.  But everyone appreciates being seen, heard, understood, and supported.  When you take the time to connect, you show you’re wired differently. You’re the hand up who doesn't approach with their hand out.This approach stands out because it’s incredibly rare.  Most of the LinkedIn lurkers who cross your path focus on taking. Which makes them utterly forgettable. Prioritize trust and connection and you automatically shift the dynamic.  It's how you graduate from the lip-snarled, eyebrow-raised, sideways glance at your connection request in their inbox to the 'OMG, this person is so helpful and they want to connect with me!?' can't accept fast enough response.  ---## Showing Up the No-Pitch Way  Every action you take is a chance to demonstrate you care enough to show up differently, without a 'you first' agenda.Before you even request to connect, think about how you can serve them value.  Grab an article, a resource, or a fresh perspective on a challenge they’re facing and offer to share it. Just make sure it's not a thinly veiled 'buy my thing' attempt when you do.Make your connection request personal. Reference something specific about their profile that caught your attention.  Say, for example, they shared a post that resonated with you. Mention why it stood out when you reach out. This is a clear signal you’re interested in building connection and having deeper conversations.Ask their opinion about something they're uniquely qualified to give. Invite them into a conversation that’s meaningful and interesting to both of you.  Build rapport naturally. That's your only agenda.Creating content is another way you can practice the No-Pitch Philosophy and attraction model.  Make your posts about your audience. More 'you' than 'me'. Share insights, tell stories, and solve problems.  A prime example that creates lively engagement? Write about a common mistake you see in your industry and how to avoid it.  Posts like these not only position you as a trusted resource but also allow people in your network or industry to flex their know-how by contributing to the conversation. It's a one-two punch that sits at the top of my content play list and one I almost always recommend.The beauty of this approach is that it compounds over time. Each thoughtful interaction, each piece of value-driven content, builds your reputation as someone worth knowing, listening to, and working with.---And that's a wrap on my No-Pitch Philosophy. Deceptively simple, isn't it?  No-Pitch your way to connection. Give a sh\*t. Lead with integrity. Build trust. Become magnetic. Let opportunities find you.  Those are the six best practices I recommend to use while you navigate today's LinkedIn landscape. Now it's time to learn how to plug it into the system itself...
```

## A: 
# Chapter 8: Creating Your Client-Attracting Profile

Your LinkedIn profile acts like your first handshake with prospects. Or, a fist bump if that's more your style.

It’s where curiosity turns into connection. Think of it as your personal billboard, without hoping someone catches a glimpse of it while flying by on the highway at 65 mph.

Do it well, and it draws all the eyes and attention of your ideals straight to you.

Start treating your profile like a funnel to make it easy for high-quality, problem aware solution seekers to tap your virtual shoulder to ask for an assist.

Follow the actionable steps in this chapter and you'll transform your profile from passive digital real estate into your client-attracting calling card.

* * *

## Optimizing Your Profile for Success

Your LinkedIn profile is your chance to command attention and build curiosity in milliseconds. To make them count, you need to optimize every section and keep the 'right' eyes reading it.

**It starts with your headline.**

Treat it like your hook to make it irresistible.

Skip titles like 'Freelance Consultant' that are open to interpretation. Instead, focus on outcomes you deliver.

Clarity in your headline sets the tone for the entire profile and tells your audience why they should keep reading.

**Make your summary conversational, not a corporate mission statement.**

Open with a a relatable challenge your ideal clients face and position yourself as the guide with an effective way to solve it. Then, close with a clear call to action.

A summary that reads like a real-life conversation would sound compels those you want to keep reading along if you weave in a storyline they can see themselves into it.

**Use your experience section to highlight results.**

Don’t just list job duties and responsibilities here. Instead, show how you’ve delivered value and results you've helped your clients achieve.

Metrics are what turn a bland job description into proof of your expertise, so don't be afraid to use them to your advantage.

It's not egotistical. It's tangible data that backs your wisdom and helps you flex your credibility muscle.

**Finally, treat your photos and visuals as the important part of your story that they are.**

A headshot from a professional builds more trust than any filtered selfie ever will.

Add a banner that reflects your brand identity and puts your solution in the spotlight to make your profile look polished and intentional.

Follow these guidelines so every detail works together to propel you to 'top of mind' status for your ideals.

* * *

## A Detailed Guide to Crafting Your Perfect Profile

Someone just landed on your profile page.

Will they understand who you are, what you do, and why you’re the perfect partner for their business right away? If you're unsure, they are too. 

Make it loud and clear. Use this step by step guide to do it. 

### Create a Headline That Captivates

Your headline is the first thing people see. Make sure you make it count.

Focus on outcomes delivered for the people you serve. Use a simple structure like this to write yours:

_'Helping coaches attract clients in 90 days with magnetic personal branding strategies.'_

Remember, a compelling headline highlights your unique value proposition, piques curiosity, and invites your ideal prospect to explore more.

### Keep Your Summary Conversational and Direct

Leverage the summary section of your profile to showcase your personality alongside your value.

It’s your elevator pitch, but you'll want to keep it natural and approachable. Avoid industry jargon and write it like you'd say it to your ideal client.

**Pro tip:** when you're finished read your final version out loud to make sure it 'sounds like you'.

Start with a compelling scenario that showcases a problem your clients hire you to help them solve. Focus on their 'now' dilemma and their desired 'future' feeling, which is way more powerful than the tangible outcome.

Then, position yourself as the bridge. Keep it believable when you add a key feature and benefit statement about your solution.  

Here's an example to help you get started:

_"You're not alone if attracting high-quality leads on LinkedIn is a struggle. More often than not, it's not you, it's your profile. Service providers seek me out to create profiles that draw in their dream clients fast. And I'm here to deliver the same for you. Let's connect to make your profile irresistible."_

I know you've heard it before, but it's worth a reminder here. Emotions sell, logic justifies a decision to buy. Why wouldn't you lean into how your ideals want to feel if partnering with you delivers it? 

### Turn Your Experience Into a Client Magnet

As for your experience section, make it make your case. To do that might take a bit of a reframe for you.

Reject the oh so popular practice and tempting urge to regurgitate a resume-style list here. If someone wants details like that, they'll send a connection request to ask for it, honestly.

Instead, frame each role in terms of the value you delivered for clients or employers.

This is the spot you want to focus on measurable, tangible outcomes and flex your metrics with descriptions like these:

_"Developed a LinkedIn outreach strategy that increased leads by 200% in three months"_

_"Helped startups realize positive revenue growth month over month with targeted social campaigns"_ 

_"Increased conversion rates by 40% with targeted outreach strategies"_

_"Boosted visibility with a 1438% growth in connections in 6 months"_

When you leverage your experience section this way, after seeing the first few lines of your job summaries, ideal prospects convince themselves they need you in their business.

### Optimize Your URL to Make Referrals Easy

A small detail as simple as a URL can make a huge difference.

Customize your LinkedIn URL to include your name or business name for a clean, professional look. A memorable, on brand URL enhances your credibility and makes it easier for your network to share your profile with others.

You can take it one step further if you own a domain name you're known for too. Shorten the LinkedIn URL you share to www.yourdomain.com/LinkedIn and redirect your profile page to it.

In short, use a congruent URL for your profile to maximize the number and frequency of referrals you get.

### Treat Your Visuals Like A Book Cover

First impressions count. Ask any promising author with underwhelming sales if their covers are possibly more important than their prose as far as their books are concerned.

Don't even get me started on the big names. Corporate branding is a multi-billion dollar investment year after year.

Give your brand imagery the attention it deserves because it's what commands the attention you seek.

Invest in a high-quality headshot that’s professional yet approachable.

Leave the decade-old headshots for your scrapbook though. You'll want to use a photo that accurately represents how you look today.

It allows you to build 'trust at first sight' if they meet you for a virtual call or see your video content in their feed.

Stuck without a recent headshot? Background removers and generative AI today can turn an everyday close up of your face into a quality portrait in no time, so no excuses.

Your banner, on the other hand, should reflect your brand—whether that’s showcasing your tagline, core services, or a memorable quote. Keep 'on brand' with colors, fonts, and voice to tie everything into a memorable package. Brand recognition, even on a small scale, can take you farther than you think.

By optimizing your LinkedIn profile with these steps, you tell your story at a glance. Your ideal prospects will thank you for it (or at least find you faster because of it).

* * *

## The Power of SEO on LinkedIn

Think of LinkedIn SEO kind of like a discovery tripwire.

Weave the right keywords into your profile and you lay the trigger that can explode a landmine of high-quality traffic to your solutions.

All it takes is for your ideal client to search those keywords in the LinkedIn toolbar and, boom, your name pops up.

Start with your headline and summary.

Use terms your ideal clients are most likely to type into LinkedIn’s search bar. Phrases like "B2B lead generation expert" or "startup funding strategist" make great choices.

Just remember, keyword stuffing is a turnoff. Focus on naturally weaving them throughout your profile so people continue to read it.

Mirror this approach in your experience section. Highlight key phrases alongside the measurable results mentioned earlier, such as "Increased SaaS lead generation by 150% using targeted LinkedIn outreach."

When your profile speaks their language, it tells prospects they’ve found the right fit.

Even your skills section plays a role with SEO.

Select skills that align with your expertise and your target audience’s needs. Encourage endorsements from people in your network and previous clients to reinforce your credibility.

Every keyword you include strengthens your profile’s search visibility.

SEO is about intention. It doesn't need to be overwhelming.

When you get into your ideal client's head, consider what they need and the words they use when they search for solves, you position yourself to land right before their eyes.

* * *

Your LinkedIn profile can be your most powerful client-attraction tool once you know how to use it.

The next time a prospect lands on your page, give them something more than a glorified resume to look at. Allow them to see you as the answer to their problem.

Now that you know how to optimize your profile, go do it so you're ready for what comes next...Finding the right audience to land on your page.

The conclusion has been updated with a transition sentence leading into the next chapter about finding your target audience:

**"And now that your profile is optimized, it’s time to learn how to find the right audience to land on it."**

Let me know if any further adjustments are needed!

Use a simple structure like this to write yours:*"Helping coaches attract clients in 90 days with magnetic personal branding strategies."*Remember, a compelling headline highlights your unique value proposition, piques curiosity, and invites your ideal prospect to explore more.### Keep Your Summary Conversational and DirectLeverage the summary section of your profile to showcase your personality alongside your value.  It’s your elevator pitch, but you'll want to keep it natural and approachable. Avoid industry jargon and write it like you'd say it to your ideal client.  **Pro tip:** When you're finished, read your final version out loud to make sure it 'sounds like you.'Start with a compelling scenario that showcases a problem your clients hire you to help them solve. Focus on their 'now' dilemma and their desired 'future' feeling, which is way more powerful than the tangible outcome.  Then, position yourself as the bridge. Keep it believable when you add a key feature and benefit statement about your solution.  Here's an example to help you get started:  *"You're not alone if attracting high-quality leads on LinkedIn is a struggle. More often than not, it's not you, it's your profile. Service providers seek me out to create profiles that draw in their dream clients fast. And I'm here to deliver the same for you. Let's connect to make your profile irresistible."*I know you've heard it before, but it's worth a reminder here. Emotions sell, logic justifies a decision to buy. Why wouldn't you lean into how your ideals want to feel if partnering with you delivers it?  ---## The Power of SEO on LinkedInThink of LinkedIn SEO kind of like a discovery tripwire.Weave the right keywords into your profile and you lay the trigger that can explode a landmine of high-quality traffic to your solutions.  All it takes is for your ideal client to search those keywords in the LinkedIn toolbar and, boom, your name pops up.Start with your headline and summary.  Use terms your ideal clients are most likely to type into LinkedIn’s search bar. Phrases like "B2B lead generation expert" or "startup funding strategist" make great choices.  Just remember, keyword stuffing is a turnoff. Focus on naturally weaving them throughout your profile so people continue to read it.Mirror this approach in your experience section. Highlight key phrases alongside the measurable results mentioned earlier, such as "Increased SaaS lead generation by 150% using targeted LinkedIn outreach."  When your profile speaks their language, it tells prospects they’ve found the right fit.Even your skills section plays a role with SEO.  Select skills that align with your expertise and your target audience’s needs. Encourage endorsements from people in your network and previous clients to reinforce your credibility.  Every keyword you include strengthens your profile’s search visibility.SEO is about intention. It doesn't need to be overwhelming.  When you get into your ideal client's head, consider what they need and the words they use when they search for solutions, you position yourself to land right before their eyes.---Your LinkedIn profile can be your most powerful client-attraction tool once you know how to use it.  The next time a prospect lands on your page, give them something more than a glorified resume to look at. Allow them to see you as the answer to their problem.  Now that you know how to optimize your profile, go do it so you're ready for what comes next...Finding the right audience to land on your page.
```

Let me know if it’s ready for submission!

## A: 
# \# Chapter 9: Finding Your Target Audience

  

LinkedIn can either feel like you fell into a black hole or stumbled upon a gold mine.

  

Knowing exactly who you’re trying to reach will be what determines your fate.

  

When you’re clear on your target audience, you stop contributing to the noise. You connect with the people who can benefit most from your expertise.

  

Follow along and see how to define, refine, and search LinkedIn so you can connect with those you're most aligned to serve and inside your own gold mine.

  

\---

  

\## How To Nail Your ICP And Why It Matters

  

Before diving feet first into LinkedIn searches or Sales Navigator, take a minute.

  

Because your ICP can be a absolute treasure map when you get it right.

  

Yet somehow, I continue to see business owners stuff spreadsheets full of random and unrelated job titles in their attempt to create decent prospecting lists.

  

And, if they would just answer some simple questions to define who they're really trying to reach, those lists could be way more valuable.

  

So, since you have the benefit of reading this now, these are the questions you might want to consider answering before you even think about entering a single name onto your prospect list.

  

\*\*What demographics do your ideal clients belong to?\*\*

  

Your baseline data here includes industries, job roles, and geographic location.

  

\*\*What are your ideal client\*\* \*\*psychographics?\*\*

  

This is where you explore deeper motivations, goals, and challenges behind their behavior.

  

Consider their pain points. List the trends they follow. State their beliefs and core values.

  

\*\*How do they show up on LinkedIn?\*\*

  

Determine if your ideal clients are more active on the platform and post regularly, or if they're more passive but show up consistently to engage with others' content.

  

With answers to these three questions, you'll have a strong understanding of who your ideal clients are. Which ultimately makes identifying the best people to connect with a whole lot easier, since they'll have similar qualities.

  

In this case, this prospected list of 'bests' is most likely to engage in some of your best conversations.

  

You get a deeper understanding about what makes your prospects tick because of your track record of great conversations, making every time you connect in the future that much more meaningful.

  

\---

  

\## Prospecting Without Sales Navigator

  

LinkedIn offers powerful ways to find and engage with your ideal audience, premium tools or not.

  

If you're just starting out prospecting on the platform, here's a short list of the features you can use to make your most stellar connections.

  

\*\*LinkedIn Filtered Searches\*\* are a great way to start your list.

  

Use this feature to sort people of the platform by their industry, location, and current role to narrow your results.

  

You can get more specific in your search filters and look for people who work at a specific company now or a company they've worked at in the past, school they attended, or language they use on their profile.

  

Filtered searches can also help you find people that match your ideal client psychographics with a search for followers of a specific brand or personality on the platform as well as a designated keyword search.

  

\*\*LinkedIn Events\*\* can be a low-lift way to engage with a group or community looking to solve for a specific problem or make progress on an important goal.

  

If you're already connected to people on the platform, you've likely been invited to a LinkedIn event they've hosted. Accepting the most relevant invitations from connections when they fit your schedule is a double win.

  

First, you get to observe and engage in a discussion that matters to people who are most likely your ideal clients. Ask thoughtful questions and contribute to the conversation to build your credibility and boost your KLT factor.

  

Second, being their is a vote of support for the event host. Adding your unique perspective or expertise to the narrative without 'stealing the spotlight' shows you genuinely want the host to win. That alone makes you a natural go-to on their refer-a-pro speed dial list when someone they know needs someone like you to solve a problem.

  

Finally, tap into \*\*LinkedIn Groups.\*\* If you gave an honorary role to Groups in your business, you could easily call them your prospecting intern.

  

Join groups where your ICP might hang out, and engage consistently by adding your unique take to discussions and bridging understanding gaps in your area of expertise.

  

My advice is to get into your dashboard right away and play with these three ways to build a prospect list that's fit for your business to see how you fare. Because, as effective as these free tools are, they do come with limitations. And when you bump up against those, you'll want to consider an upgrade to your next-level prospecting pal, Sales Navigator.

  

\---

  

\## Unleash the Sales Navigator Beast

  

As cliche as it sounds, if free tools like Groups are your prospecting intern, Sales Navigator would be your VP of Business Development.

  

And a VP does come with a price tag. The good news is, adding a great VP to your team earns far more than their keep, even with generous compensation plans.

  

All this to say, adding Sales Navigator to your tool kit unlocks precision targeting so you have a finely-tuned list of aligned people to engage and build relationships with.

  

No, Navigator is not just some way they devised to monetize the LinkedIn platform. Ads do plenty in that department.

  

Specifically, the \*\*advanced filters and Boolean search\*\* features you unlock when you subscribe allow you to refine your criteria beyond the basics.

  

For example, say you need to find decision-makers in tech startups that generate $5M–$10M annually. Sales Navigator makes it easy to find them. Boolean search allows you to create ultra-specific criteria, ensuring you reach exactly the right audience.

  

Other standout Navigator features include \*\*lead lists and intent data,\*\* whether you use them separately or in tandem. Combined, they're like having a private eye on your payroll who creates dynamic lists that track potential clients to keep tabs on their intent activity.

  

Intent signals, like recent posts or profile updates, show who’s actively engaging and ready to connect. This prioritization ensures your outreach is both efficient and effective.

  

Of course, LinkedIn combines the power of these upgraded features behind the scenes with a reward for paid subscribers they call \*\*recommended leads\*\*.

  

These are lists of 100 connections they suggest to you that you may not have discovered otherwise. They're algorithm-driven, auto-generated prospect lists based on your search history, saved preferences, and intent signals. Smart way to keep you paying for the added features if you think about it.

  

If all those features and benefits aren't enough to help you justify investing in Navigator, I've got one more that might get you off the fence.

  

\*\*Pro tip\*\*: Sales Navigator users experience relaxed account restrictions. Not officially, but in our agency experience, subscribers are allowed higher volume penalty-free outreach.

  

Okay, I lied. I've got two closing arguments for the upgrade...

  

Sales Navigator has a \*\*30-day free trial\*\* for new users. Try it out. If you love it, keep it.

  

It's how you 'hire' a stand-in for your VP of Business Development for a full year for less than cost of one week's payroll to fill that role with top talent. When leveraged effectively, it could help you fund your future head of business development hire too.

  

\---

  

\## Targeting Smart, Not Wide With TAM

  

Knowing your total addressable market (TAM for short) ensures you’re you’re fishing where the fish are instead of casting a wide net into murky, barren waters.

  

To start you'll determine your market size on LinkedIn. You'll do that by searching for users who match your ICP. Save this search so you can track changes to this number over time.

  

From there, break your TAM into smaller, actionable segments so you can prioritize your outreach.

  

Focus on \*\*second-degree connections\*\*, as they're your warmest leads by far. Here’s how to rank your leads like your yearbook did, with most likely to succeed at the top:

  

1\. \*\*Prime Prospects:\*\* Second-degree connections who posted on LinkedIn in the last 30 days and match your geographic focus. These leads are highly engaged and ready for outreach.

2\. \*\*Strong Opportunities:\*\* Second-degree connections who have been active recently but may fall outside your geographic focus.

3\. \*\*Emerging Targets:\*\* Second-degree connections who match your ICP but haven’t posted recently. While less active, they still fit your profile.

  

When you rank your TAM to prioritize the most active, engaged, 2nd degree connections, you'll save yourself a bunch of time and energy. It's the best advice I can give that allows you to invest 'minimum effort' for 'maximum results' on LinkedIn.

  

\---

  

With a clear ICP in mind, strategic use of LinkedIn tools, and a ranked TAM outreach approach, you can finally kick that feeling of shouting into the void.

  

You’ll have more conversations with the right-for-you people that lead to real opportunities.

  

But when you make first contact, it's important to know what to say to turn new connections into collaborations. Good thing messaging strategy is on the docket next...

The chapter has been rewritten to align with the **15-point checklist**, addressing the following:

*   **H2 improvements**: Removed colons and made them more dynamic.
    
*   **Narrative flow**: Expanded bullet-heavy sections into engaging narratives, particularly in the TAM section.
    
*   **Simplified technical concepts**: Clarified terms like Boolean search and audience ranking for better beginner accessibility.
    
*   **Enhanced tone**: Maintained Braden’s conversational, approachable style throughout.
    

Please review the revised version and let me know if further adjustments are needed!

```
# Chapter 9: Finding Your Target AudienceLinkedIn can either feel like you fell into a black hole or stumbled upon a gold mine.Knowing exactly who you’re trying to reach will be what determines your fate.When you’re clear on your target audience, you stop contributing to the noise. You connect with the people who can benefit most from your expertise.Follow along and see how to define, refine, and search LinkedIn so you can connect with those you're most aligned to serve and inside your own gold mine.---## How To Nail Your ICP And Why It MattersBefore diving feet first into LinkedIn searches or Sales Navigator, take a minute.Because your ICP can be an absolute treasure map when you get it right.Yet somehow, I continue to see business owners stuff spreadsheets full of random and unrelated job titles in their attempt to create decent prospecting lists.And, if they would just answer some simple questions to define who they're really trying to reach, those lists could be way more valuable.So, since you have the benefit of reading this now, these are the questions you might want to consider answering before you even think about entering a single name onto your prospect list.**What demographics do your ideal clients belong to?**Your baseline data here includes industries, job roles, and geographic location.**What are your ideal client psychographics?**This is where you explore deeper motivations, goals, and challenges behind their behavior.Consider their pain points. List the trends they follow. State their beliefs and core values.**How do they show up on LinkedIn?**Determine if your ideal clients are more active on the platform and post regularly, or if they're more passive but show up consistently to engage with others' content.With answers to these three questions, you'll have a strong understanding of who your ideal clients are. Which ultimately makes identifying the best people to connect with a whole lot easier, since they'll have similar qualities.In this case, this prospected list of 'bests' is most likely to engage in some of your best conversations.You get a deeper understanding about what makes your prospects tick because of your track record of great conversations, making every time you connect in the future that much more meaningful.---## Prospecting Without Sales NavigatorLinkedIn offers powerful ways to find and engage with your ideal audience, premium tools or not.If you're just starting out prospecting on the platform, here's a short list of the features you can use to make your most stellar connections.**LinkedIn Filtered Searches** are a great way to start your list.Use this feature to sort people of the platform by their industry, location, and current role to narrow your results.You can get more specific in your search filters and look for people who work at a specific company now or a company they've worked at in the past, school they attended, or language they use on their profile.Filtered searches can also help you find people that match your ideal client psychographics with a search for followers of a specific brand or personality on the platform as well as a designated keyword search.**LinkedIn Events** can be a low-lift way to engage with a group or community looking to solve for a specific problem or make progress on an important goal.If you're already connected to people on the platform, you've likely been invited to a LinkedIn event they've hosted. Accepting the most relevant invitations from connections when they fit your schedule is a double win.First, you get to observe and engage in a discussion that matters to people who are most likely your ideal clients. Ask thoughtful questions and contribute to the conversation to build your credibility and boost your KLT factor.Second, being there is a vote of support for the event host. Adding your unique perspective or expertise to the narrative without 'stealing the spotlight' shows you genuinely want the host to win. That alone makes you a natural go-to on their refer-a-pro speed dial list when someone they know needs someone like you to solve a problem.Finally, tap into **LinkedIn Groups.** If you gave an honorary role to Groups in your business, you could easily call them your prospecting intern.Join groups where your ICP might hang out, and engage consistently by adding your unique take to discussions and bridging understanding gaps in your area of expertise.My advice is to get into your dashboard right away and play with these three ways to build a prospect list that's fit for your business to see how you fare. Because, as effective as these free tools are, they do come with limitations. And when you bump up against those, you'll want to consider an upgrade to your next-level prospecting pal, Sales Navigator.---## Unleash the Sales Navigator BeastAs cliché as it sounds, if free tools like Groups are your prospecting intern, Sales Navigator would be your VP of Business Development.And a VP does come with a price tag. The good news is, adding a great VP to your team earns far more than their keep, even with generous compensation plans.All this to say, adding Sales Navigator to your toolkit unlocks precision targeting so you have a finely-tuned list of aligned people to engage and build relationships with.Specifically, the **advanced filters and Boolean search** features you unlock when you subscribe allow you to refine your criteria beyond the basics.For example, say you need to find decision-makers in tech startups that generate $5M–$10M annually. Sales Navigator makes it easy to find them. Boolean search allows you to create ultra-specific criteria, ensuring you reach exactly the right audience.Other standout Navigator features include **lead lists and intent data,** whether you use them separately or in tandem. Combined, they're like having a private eye on your payroll who creates dynamic lists that track potential clients to keep tabs on their intent activity.Intent signals, like recent posts or profile updates, show who’s actively engaging and ready to connect. This prioritization ensures your outreach is both efficient and effective.Of course, LinkedIn combines the power of these upgraded features behind the scenes with a reward for paid subscribers they call **recommended leads**.These are lists of 100 connections they suggest to you that you may not have discovered otherwise. They're algorithm-driven, auto-generated prospect lists based on your search history, saved preferences, and intent signals. Smart way to keep you paying for the added features if you think about it.If all those features and benefits aren't enough to help you justify investing in Navigator, I've got one more that might get you off the fence.**Pro tip**: Sales Navigator users experience relaxed account restrictions. Not officially, but in our agency experience, subscribers are allowed higher volume penalty-free outreach.Okay, I lied. I've got two closing arguments for the upgrade...Sales Navigator has a **30-day free trial** for new users. Try it out. If you love it, keep it.It's how you 'hire' a stand-in for your VP of Business Development for a full year for less than cost of one week's payroll to fill that role with top talent. When leveraged effectively, it could help you fund your future head of business development hire too.---## Targeting Smart, Not Wide With TAMKnowing your total addressable market (TAM for short) ensures you’re you’re fishing where the fish are instead of casting a wide net into murky, barren waters.To start you'll determine your market size on LinkedIn. You'll do that by searching for users who match your ICP. Save this search so you can track changes to this number over time.From there, break your TAM into smaller, actionable segments so you can prioritize your outreach.Focus on **second-degree connections**, as they're your warmest leads by far. Here’s how to rank your leads like your yearbook did, with most likely to succeed at the top:1. **Prime Prospects:** Second-degree connections who posted on LinkedIn in the last 30 days and match your geographic focus. These leads are highly engaged and ready for outreach.2. **Strong Opportunities:** Second-degree connections who have been active recently but may fall outside your geographic focus.3. **Emerging Targets:** Second-degree connections who match your ICP but haven’t posted recently. While less active, they still fit your profile.When you rank your TAM to prioritize the most active, engaged, 2nd degree connections, you'll save yourself a bunch of time and energy. It's the best advice I can give that allows you to invest 'minimum effort' for 'maximum results' on LinkedIn.---With a clear ICP in mind, strategic use of LinkedIn tools, and a ranked TAM outreach approach, you can finally kick that feeling of shouting into the void.You’ll have more conversations with the right-for-you people that lead to real opportunities.But when you make first contact, it's important to know what to say to turn new connections into collaborations. Good thing messaging strategy is on the docket next...
