## A: 
\# \*\*Chapter 10: The Outreach System\*\*

  

Finally and undoubtedly, you made it to the backbone of my entire LinkedIn fast track to successful lead generation strategy, The Outreach System. It’s how you get to elevate connection from an art form into a predictable science.

  

The science of lead-getting doesn’t mean you hide inside a sterile lab coat and follow a sterile script over and over, day after day. In fact, to build real, long-term partnerships with this system, you’ll need to break out of rigid routines and allow for natural flow.

  

Follow this step-by-step process, from first connection request onward and you’ll spark relationships that go beyond the friendly confines of LinkedIn more often than not.

  

\## Step 1: Connecting to Connect

  

Nobody wants to get pitch slapped.

  

It \*\*is\*\* the best way to lose friends and not influence people, unless your goal is to p\*ss them off.

  

So please, do yourself a favor and just stop the pitch-fest connection requests, okay?

  

As Fontana reports to Burgundy, 60% of the time it works every time.  
  
[RELEVANT GIF OF RON BURGUNDY MOVIE GOES HERE]  
  
If you’re not good with that math or those odds, the solution is a pretty simple one.

  

Invite a conversation. Open a channel. Find your common ground.

  

I call it adopting a “Connecting to Connect” mindset, or put another way, a ‘just because’ conversation. Quite refreshing compared to the ‘zero to pay me in five sentences flat’ approach, isn’t it?

  

Here’s how you do it.

  

Keep your connection request short, sweet, and personal. Tell them what genuinely caught your attention on their profile or in a recent post.

  

Your only goal is to convey a vibe that resonates for you both. When you give just to give, people feel the difference, and remember you. Exceptions are always more memorable. Be the pattern interrupt.

  

Given these two connection requests waiting in your inbox, which one are you most likely to accept?

  

<aside>

  

\*Hi [Name], I specialize in helping businesses grow using [service]. Let me know if you’d be open to a call to discuss how I can help your business!\*

  

</aside>

  

\*\*Or…\*\*

  

<aside>

  

\*Hi [Name], I came across your profile after reading your post on [topic], and I really appreciated your perspective on [specific point]. I’d love to connect and continue the conversation if you’re open to it.\*

  

</aside>

  

I hope I made it glaringly obvious by now, but just in case I didn’t, you’d do ‘the two’, right?

  

In which case, show up like that second message in your outreach, and see what happens.

  

Or choose number one and prepare for a stretch of connectionless days.

  

\## \*\*Step 2: Craft Connection Requests That Resonate\*\*

  

Your connection request is like your first handshake. You want it to feel confident, not clammy. Here’s how to nail it every time:

  

\- \*\*Personalize:\*\* Start by referencing a shared interest, a recent post they made, or a common connection. It shows you’re paying attention and not just sending a mass invite.

\- \*\*Keep It Concise:\*\* LinkedIn isn’t a novel-writing platform. Aim for two to three sentences, tops.

\- \*\*Be Authentic:\*\* People can smell insincerity a mile away. If you can’t find a real reason to connect, don’t force it.

  

\*\*Pro Tip\*\*: Sometimes, leaving the connection note blank works best, especially for 2nd-degree connections who’ve been active in the last 30 days.

  

Now, take this formula and deploy it every day. Send your 50 connection requests, and when they respond, follow up with your sequence.

  

\## \*\*Step 3: Effective Follow-Ups That Break Through the Noise\*\*

  

Your follow-up is where you build the bridge from connection to conversation. The secret sauce? Timing, value, and curiosity.

  

\- \*\*Timing:\*\* Don’t come in hot with a message right after they accept. Give it a day or two to let the connection breathe.

\- \*\*Value-Driven Content:\*\* Share something that’s genuinely useful to them like an article, a tool, or even a thoughtful insight.

\- \*\*Ask Open-Ended Questions:\*\* End your message with a question that sparks dialogue. For example,

<aside>

\*“I noticed you work in [industry]. Lately my clients say [specific issue] is their biggest challenge. Have you noticed the same thing and found an effective work around for it yet? If so I’d love to hear more about it.”\*

</aside>

  

When done right, your follow-ups will stand out as helpful and engaging, instead of pushy or plain-vanilla.

  

\## \*\*Step 4: Differentiation Tactics That Wow\*\*

  

LinkedIn inboxes are crowded. To separate yourself from the pack, you need to be a little ‘extra’. But, be the good kind of extra.

  

\- \*\*Video Messaging:\*\* A short, personalized video introducing yourself can be a game-changer. It’s personal, memorable, and shows effort.

\- \*\*Audio Notes:\*\* If video feels like too much, consider a quick voice message. It adds a human touch that text alone doesn’t.

\- \*\*Creative Personalization:\*\* Use their profile to find small details or clues, like a favorite hobby or a shared alma mater to weave naturally into your message.

  

These ‘extras’ may take a bit more time, but the ROI on successful connections makes it worth the effort.

  

\## \*\*Stay Tuned To Meet Your New Best Friend\*\*

  

The one who’s faster to execute on your outreach, but not in a sloppy, hack-job way…

  

But first, you’ve got this system. Settle in and get comfortable with it.

  

Send your requests. Craft thoughtful follow-ups. Personalize your approach.

  

Because once you nail down this outreach habit, you can scale it the low-lift way.

  

\---

  

Stay tuned for a secret weapon to make this system run like clockwork for you every single day on LinkedIn.

  

I’ll show you how you can fast-track ‘all of that’ without losing the human touch soon enough.

  

For now, I’ll tackle how you can amplify your lead-getting efforts and aligned connection results based on how you show up in their feed.

  

It’s time to launch and keep you cruising comfortably in top of mind status with your ideals.

STEP 4 for Chapter 9 is complete. A new canvas has been created for Chapter 10. Please provide the draft or input for Chapter 10, and I’ll begin the review process. Let’s continue!

## Q: 
I need to clear something up for you. Hyphenated words are different than hyphenated sentences to combine two thoughts grammatically. You can change the grade for rule 3 to a pass. Also, the example you gave for rule 15 is not a violation. In fact it's a revision of the old version that was a violation. Rule 15 is only a violation when it appears implicitly as any of these formats: [Thing] is not [description]. [Thing] is [secondary description]. [Thing] isn't about [description]. It's about [secondary description]. [Thing] isn't about [description]-it's about [secondary description]. With that in mind, does this chapter, update your analysis and % passing grade against the 15 point checklist please.

```
# Chapter 10: The Outreach SystemFinally and undoubtedly, you made it to the backbone of my entire LinkedIn fast track to successful lead generation strategy, The Outreach System. It’s how you get to elevate connection from an art form into a predictable science.The science of lead-getting doesn’t mean you hide inside a sterile lab coat and follow a sterile script over and over, day after day. In fact, to build real, long-term partnerships with this system, you’ll need to break out of rigid routines and allow for natural flow.Follow this step-by-step process, from first connection request onward, and you’ll spark relationships that go beyond the friendly confines of LinkedIn more often than not.---## Step 1: Connecting to ConnectNobody wants to get pitch slapped.It **is** the best way to lose friends and not influence people, unless your goal is to p*ss them off.So please, do yourself a favor and just stop the pitch-fest connection requests, okay?As Fontana reports to Burgundy, 60% of the time it works every time.  [RELEVANT GIF OF RON BURGUNDY MOVIE GOES HERE]If you’re not good with that math or those odds, the solution is a pretty simple one.Invite a conversation. Open a channel. Find your common ground.I call it adopting a “Connecting to Connect” mindset, or put another way, a ‘just because’ conversation. Quite refreshing compared to the ‘zero to pay me in five sentences flat’ approach, isn’t it?Here’s how you do it.Keep your connection request short, sweet, and personal. Tell them what genuinely caught your attention on their profile or in a recent post.Your only goal is to convey a vibe that resonates for you both. When you give just to give, people feel the difference and remember you. Exceptions are always more memorable. Be the pattern interrupt.Given these two connection requests waiting in your inbox, which one are you most likely to accept?<aside>*Hi [Name], I specialize in helping businesses grow using [service]. Let me know if you’d be open to a call to discuss how I can help your business!*</aside>**Or…**<aside>*Hi [Name], I came across your profile after reading your post on [topic], and I really appreciated your perspective on [specific point]. I’d love to connect and continue the conversation if you’re open to it.*</aside>I hope I made it glaringly obvious by now, but just in case I didn’t, you’d do ‘the two,’ right?In which case, show up like that second message in your outreach, and see what happens.Or choose number one and prepare for a stretch of connectionless days.---## Step 2: Craft Connection Requests That ResonateYour connection request is like your first handshake. You want it to feel confident, not clammy. Here’s how to nail it every time:- **Personalize:** Start by referencing a shared interest, a recent post they made, or a common connection. It shows you’re paying attention and not just sending a mass invite.- **Keep It Concise:** LinkedIn isn’t a novel-writing platform. Aim for two to three sentences, tops.- **Be Authentic:** People can smell insincerity a mile away. If you can’t find a real reason to connect, don’t force it.**Pro Tip**: Sometimes, leaving the connection note blank works best, especially for 2nd-degree connections who’ve been active in the last 30 days.Now, take this formula and deploy it every day. Send your 50 connection requests, and when they respond, follow up with your sequence.---## Step 3: Effective Follow-Ups That Break Through the NoiseYour follow-up is where you build the bridge from connection to conversation. The secret sauce? Timing, value, and curiosity.- **Timing:** Don’t come in hot with a message right after they accept. Give it a day or two to let the connection breathe.- **Value-Driven Content:** Share something that’s genuinely useful to them like an article, a tool, or even a thoughtful insight.- **Ask Open-Ended Questions:** End your message with a question that sparks dialogue. For example,<aside>*"I noticed you work in [industry]. Lately my clients say [specific issue] is their biggest challenge. Have you noticed the same thing and found an effective workaround for it yet? If so, I’d love to hear more about it."*</aside>When done right, your follow-ups will stand out as helpful and engaging, instead of pushy or plain-vanilla.---## Step 4: Differentiation Tactics That WowLinkedIn inboxes are crowded. To separate yourself from the pack, you need to be a little ‘extra.’ But be the good kind of extra.- **Video Messaging:** A short, personalized video introducing yourself can be a game-changer. It’s personal, memorable, and shows effort.- **Audio Notes:** If video feels like too much, consider a quick voice message. It adds a human touch that text alone doesn’t.- **Creative Personalization:** Use their profile to find small details or clues, like a favorite hobby or a shared alma mater, to weave naturally into your message.These ‘extras’ may take a bit more time, but the ROI on successful connections makes it worth the effort.---## Stay Tuned To Meet Your New Best FriendThe one who’s faster to execute on your outreach, but not in a sloppy, hack-job way…But first, you’ve got this system. Settle in and get comfortable with it.Send your requests. Craft thoughtful follow-ups. Personalize your approach.  Because once you nail down this outreach habit, you can scale it the low-lift way.  ---Stay tuned for a secret weapon to make this system run like clockwork for you every single day on LinkedIn.I’ll show you how you can fast-track ‘all of that’ without losing the human touch soon enough.For now, I’ll tackle how you can amplify your lead-getting efforts and aligned connection results based on how you show up in their feed.It’s time to launch and keep you cruising comfortably in top-of-mind status with your ideals.
```

And so when people are commenting on yours and they're liking yours, it will help your post get more exposure. Also the 8020 rule, uh, I like to look at this as relationships. If you were, if you are in a relationship and you're 100% nice all of the time, or you're 100% sassy all the time, I imagine that's Katie, um, or you are, you know, 100% of anything all the time, the relationship generally runs its course because there's nothing keeping the other person on their toes at all. So me, I like to be 80% nice or 20% sassy. Um, or more. Um, but same thing with LinkedIn posts. Don't just do the same type of posts over and over and over and over. 80% towards stories and towards value posts. And 20% can be lead generation posts. Hey, comment this if you want my free ebook, or do this if you want. Leave your email or whatever it is. Keep people guessing because that will keep them intrigued. If you just post the same thing over and over, they're going to see that you posted, they're going to scroll right past it because they know they've gotten the same thing the last 12, 20 times that you posted. It's going to make them not want to engage with your content and make them not want to read it, thus kind of hurting your reach, hurting your ability to influence or have those people engage with your stuff. So that's my 8020 rule. And then this is a big question that we get asked is, okay, how do I go viral? Um, as with all social platforms, engagement is the number one key to going viral. My engagement, I mean getting likes, getting shares and getting comments on your posts. Um, I like to put in, I put four to five hashtags here. Generally I put in between three to five hashtags. It's not Instagram, we need to put a whole bunch. But there are ways to find content and people. Actually, do people and businesses follow hashtags? So I put in those hashtags in the related to your post. They'll actually have more of a chance that people will see that post. Um, number three, everybody who comments, comment back. LinkedIn's algorithm loves when there's a conversation going on in the comments. If somebody asks you a question, answer it. Ask them a question back. If somebody says, great post, make sure you say, thank you. The more comments that you get, the more that they feel like, hey, they're not just posting to get engagement, they're posting to actually engage. LinkedIn loves that. And they're much more likely to continue to show that because they know those other people who are taking their time to comment, they're going to get a response back from you. And then, last rule of going viral, if you have a schedule where you're saying, posting maybe four times a week, and you have one post that's doing exceptionally well from the start, you know, maybe six hours in, you have more likes, more comments, more shares, more views than you normally get. Put that second post aside. Let this one continue to run its course, because as soon as you make that second post, LinkedIn is going to say, oh, hey, we need to start putting this next post out, this most recent post. So, yes, there is that value, you know, good content piece. But there's also a fact of, uh, once you post Something else, LinkedIn will start, will stop pushing people to the first post that you made that's already doing well and start pushing people toward that second post. And if it's already doing better, that means it's a better piece of content. That means it's going to get more likes, get more views overall than a piece that is, and maybe not doing so well at the beginning. So kind of be able to tell that. ## A: 
# Chapter 11: Content Creation That Converts

Forget everything you think you know about today's social platforms, which one is best, for who and why, etc. I'm sure it was given as well-meant advice.

If, say, it wasn't from a decade ago. And, your advisor delivered it with the sole intent of selling you a proven, repeatable system for the many, not just the few who use it.

LinkedIn is the bridge between your expertise and the decision-makers who need it. To make the connection count, you need content that commands attention and delivers value.

But why LinkedIn? What makes it the ideal space for B2B content marketing exactly?

Consider these standout statistics to clue you in...

LinkedIn is the **most-used social platform among Fortune 500 companies** **and drives more than 50% of all social traffic to B2B websites** and blogs.

About **45% of LinkedIn article readers hold upper-level positions**, such as managers, VPs, directors, or C-level executives.

Additionally, **LinkedIn generates 80% of B2B leads**, compared to just 13% on Twitter and 7% on Facebook.

This isn’t just hearsay either.

These numbers come direct from the independent research reports and paint a very clear picture. LinkedIn is the ultimate B2B lead-generation engine.

When you create content tailored to LinkedIn’s audience, you’re not just broadcasting—you’re building relationships with decision-makers who actively seek out value.

The challenge? Crafting scroll-stopping posts that build trust, spark engagement, and deliver results. Before I dive into my list of the top ways you can make that happen, here's a sprinkle of what a system that leans into sharing great content on LinkedIn can do for you.

* * *

## Why Content Marketing Wins on LinkedIn

Your success on LinkedIn relies on your ability to deliver meaningful, value-driven insights to cement your position as the trusted expert.

Readers who invite you to their feed by consuming and engaging with your content are 'buying what you're selling,' so to speak.

It starts with getting to know you. Each interaction they make with your content earns a tally in your likability and credibility columns.

Eventually, those tallies compound into their acceptance of you as a trusted authority in your niche who they can see themselves doing business with once they need and are ready to invest in your solutions.

When done right, your content becomes a magnet that:

*   **Establishes Thought Leadership**: Be the go-to voice your audience trusts for clarity and guidance.
    
*   **Attracts Dream Clients**: Speak directly to the challenges your ideal clients face.
    
*   **Generates Qualified Leads**: Create conversations that evolve into lasting relationships.
    

As an added bonus, the lump sum of those interactions with your high-value content help train LinkedIn's algorithm to show more of your posts to like audiences.

Plus Linked alerts 1st level connections of your reader what their network is engaging with. Since like tends to attract like, you benefit from earning attention from an ideal prospect outside your network. And, LinkedIn benefits from more time spent engaging on their platform when they show your content to someone new who consumes what you post.

Think of your LinkedIn feed as a storefront. Each post is a window that invites prospects to step inside, learn more, and explore what you bring to the table. When your content consistently delivers value, you build an ecosystem where connection drives business and the platform rewards you for sharing.

* * *

## Master Mobile-First Content

A large majority of your audience consume your content on the go. Let me do one better and quantify what I mean by 'large.' More than 70% of LinkedIn users access the platform via mobile devices.

Optimizing your content for mobile is your mission critical. These tips are your go-to so that your posts are enticing to read away from the desktop:

*   **Start Strong**: The first two lines of your post act as the hook. Bold claims, intriguing questions, or emotional appeals grab attention immediately, especially in a fast-scrolling mobile environment.
    
*   **Visual Appeal**: Incorporate clean, high-quality visuals that are easy to interpret on small screens. This includes infographics, banners, or even slides that utilize minimalist design to get your point across.
    
*   **Keep it Snackable**: Dense text can overwhelm mobile users, especially if they're multi-tasking like most are when they use their phones. Break up long paragraphs into bite-sized chunks and use line breaks liberally to make your main points easy to ID and your content skimmable.
    
*   **Engage Thoughtfully**: Questions or using clear call-to-action posts work exceptionally well on mobile. A one-thumb required audience engagement by design means you’re doing it right.
    

Mobile-first is an action you take to meet your audience where they are. It shows them you respect how they want to interact on the platform.

If you haven't already adopted this best practices short list, now's the time. Give it a go to be pleasantly surprised at just how much it boosts your engagement over time. 

* * *

## The Solve, Share, Showcase Framework

Creating content that converts doesn’t have to be complicated. Use this simple framework as your quick how-to guide.

### Solve Their Problems

Lead with empathy.

Speak directly to the pain points your audience faces, then and offer actionable solutions. When you demonstrate that you understand their challenges, you build trust and loyalty.

When you craft clear, practical steps with tutorials, quick tips, or common pitfall workarounds so they can solve specific issues, you help them through. You become their 'hand up'.

### Share What Matters

Position yourself as the go-to source for what’s new, next, and critical in your industry.

Whether it’s breaking news, emerging trends, or strategic and actionable insights, valuable information they can use keeps your audience coming back for more.

Do yourself a favor. Curate content about trending topics relevant to your niche. It allows you to produce timely content that provides answers your ideal clients need, seek out, and expect from experts like you.

### Showcase Your Expertise

Expertise is a dish that's best served warm. And by warm, I mean, from your client files. 

Share success stories, behind-the-scenes insights, practical tips, and testimonials to showcase your skills, establish credibility, and boost your trust factor.

Whether it’s a checklist, a case study, or a personal anecdote, let your content do the heavy-lifting.

Montage reel of your biggest real-world wins? Yep, highly recommend.

Consistent mini-brag win posts is your goal here.

It's the celebration angle without the mega-ego vibe.

It's the tell them you're awesome without telling them you're awesome approach.

And, it's how you serve up your expertise like the decadent dessert it's meant to be guilt-free.

* * *

## Even More Proven Content Formats

Variety wins when it comes to post types and formats. Different formats do it for different segments of your audience. Keep it engaging with a mix of these:

*   **Text Posts**: aka, your storytelling playground. Use them to share lessons you've learned, industry insights, or to spark deeper conversations. Keep them concise and play with negative space and formatting to create a pattern interrupt on their scroll.
    
*   **Native Videos**: Allow your audience to see the person behind the profile. Short clips packed with a mini-tutorial, personal reflections, or quick wins work incredibly well to boost engagement.
    
*   **Articles**: Want to go deep? Articles are the perfect way to dive into complex topics and establish thought leadership while you amplify visibility at the same time.
    
*   **Documents**: Share bite-sized, actionable resources like checklists, templates, or infographics in the 'new' carousel way. They make for quick wins your audience craves and position you as the coach with the winning playbook.
    
*   **Polls**: Keep things interactive with polls to engage your audience, spark discussion, and gather insights. Polls can be the best tool ever when you want to tweak an offer or decide if an idea is worth developing, so don't be shy. Test them out to see how your audience responds to the format. 
    

By switching up your formats, your content gains broader appeal and keeps your readers engaged and intrigued. Always keep them curious, but never leave them guessing. It's a content rule to live by.

* * *

Whether you view it as the long-game or the fast-track, for B2B, LinkedIn content has its privileges.

Either way, crafting content that converts relies on a simple, repeatable 6-step formula.

Show up regularly. Share relevant trending industry info. Add value with quick win content.

Prove you're a problem solver. Invite them to engage. Mix it up so they show up.

Give to give. See what you get for your efforts.

Now that you're clear on high-converting content, I'll show you how to amplify the effect it has when you know how to package it up and deliver it in front of the right eyes at the right time.

I've made the revisions and ensured the problematic references are removed. The chapter is now updated as per your feedback. Please review and let me know if there's anything further you'd like to adjust.

LinkedIn is the ultimate B2B lead-generation engine.When you create content tailored to LinkedIn’s audience, you’re not just broadcasting—you’re building relationships with decision-makers who  actively seek out value.&#x20;The challenge? Break up long paragraphs into bite-sized chunks and use line breaks liberally to make your main points easy to ID and your content skimmable.- **Engage Thoughtfully**:  Questions or using clear call-to-action posts work exceptionally well on mobile. A one-thumb required audience engagement by design means you’re doing it right.Mobile-first is an action you take to meet your audience where they are. It shows them you respect how they want to interact on the platform.&#x20;If you haven't already adopted this best practices short list, now's the time. Thank you for pasting your original list. It aligns well with the approach needed to ensure each chapter resonates with Braden’s brand voice while maintaining strong reader engagement and clarity. Here's how we can effectively merge this into a revised crosscheck checklist for Chapter 12 and beyond, addressing all concerns with precision:

* * *

### **Updated 15-Point Crosscheck List**

1.  **Dynamic Hooks**: Open with a strong, compelling hook—no "Let’s" phrasing or weak starts. Avoid AI-like repetitive phrasing or empty hype.
    
2.  **Punchy H2s**: Ensure H2s are engaging, not generic or reliant on excessive colons. Avoid questions as hooks unless truly captivating.
    
3.  **Avoid AI-Like Patterns**: Eliminate overuse of hyphenated sentences and constructs like:
    
    *   "[Thing] isn’t [description]. It’s [alternate description]."
        
    *   "[Thing] is not about [description]. It’s about [alternate description] instead."
        
    *   "It’s not about [description]-[thing] is about [alternate description]."
        
4.  **Consistent Voice**: Maintain Braden’s friendly, conversational, and direct tone, predominantly in 2nd person, as if he’s chatting with a friend over coffee.
    
5.  **Fluid Transitions**: Ensure smooth and logical transitions between sections and ideas, free of clunky or abrupt shifts.
    
6.  **Reader-Centered Language**: Write with the audience in mind—clear, concise, and approachable for a beginner to Braden’s system.
    
7.  **True to Braden’s IP**: Support ideas with Braden’s insights and content summaries. If content gaps exist, identify the full IP source needed to strengthen the narrative.
    
8.  **No Redundancy**: Avoid repetition within the chapter and between chapters. Each section should build on the previous without overlap.
    
9.  **Full Concept Explanations**: Break down complex ideas into digestible parts without assuming prior knowledge. Write with clarity for those new to LinkedIn strategies.
    
10.  **Engaging and Fluff-Free**: Keep content substantial and focused, aiming for 1500+ words that deliver real value without padding.
    
11.  **Balanced Depth**: Offer enough detail to be actionable while avoiding overwhelming the reader with unnecessary complexity.
    
12.  **Powerful Close**: End chapters with concise, actionable takeaways and leave readers eager to implement the ideas or move to the next chapter.
    
13.  **No Outlining**: Avoid turning sections into glorified bullet-point lists. Write in fully developed paragraphs that flow naturally.
    
14.  **Exciting & Informative H2s**: Ensure H2s are varied, attention-grabbing, and meaningful without overreliance on formatting gimmicks like colons.
    
15.  **No Content Gutting**: Do not remove any user-provided material deemed spot-on or aligned with Braden’s voice without justifiable cause.
    

* * *

Would you like me to cross-check Chapter 12 again using this revised list to ensure we’ve fully aligned it? Or would you like to refine this list further before proceeding?

# Chapter 12: Running LinkedIn Events & Webinars

Imagine this.

You're the host of an event where every attendee is a decision-maker and they're excited to hear what you have to say. They accept your invite like groupies who wait in line for days to get their hands on the newest iPhone.

Maybe that's inconceivable for you based on the lackluster, thinly veiled hour-long pitchfests dressed up as important industry training you've been sucked into attending.

But, with your new 'always add value'  (chap 11 content type) framework and your expertly crafted audience from using LinkedIn filters (et all)?

Your LinkedIn events and webinars get to be your direct line to an audience that values your expertise. They prove it when they accept your invite.

Attentive AF decision makers. Feed their attention with the bites they seek so they can uplevel to clients.

It's on you to deliver [ends with grab a front row seat for the BTS on how to give your audience the show they want to see]

  

  

This chapter will take you behind the scenes of planning and executing LinkedIn events that don’t just fill seats but create real opportunities. Whether your goal is building relationships, generating leads, or claiming your spot as the go-to expert, you’ll find everything you need to make it happen.

LinkedIn events and webinars are not just another checkbox on your marketing to-do list. They are your platform to captivate decision-makers, forge meaningful relationships, and solidify your authority—all while generating high-quality leads.

When executed well, these events elevate you from just another voice in the crowd to the trusted expert everyone wants to hear from. This is your chance to stand out and showcase your expertise in real time.

Ready to unlock the full potential of LinkedIn events and webinars? Here’s your step-by-step guide to making them unforgettable and impactful.

* * *

## Why LinkedIn Events Are Worth Your Time

Let me expand on that movie goer [thread] for a sec.

Don't worry. I'm not suggesting you pull off some Herculean directorial debut with epic production value.

boring slides or generic advice aren't gonna cut it. Frame your event like a Hollywood movie premiere instead. 

A strategy that, on the surface, should equal an epic fail. 

Think about it.  tickets. concessions. time spent to and fro navigating traffic and noisy over-talkers. stream from home. yet they choose the mgx instead.

Key takeaway from that is?  

X.

Your LI attendees are there to watch you 'act out' the process they need to solve the prob they have. Tell them the how to story. Write them into the script with quick win action steps at the end.

When you deliver your X like that you give them hope. You shift into director and they take on the lead actor role. Once they see themselves in your storyline, expect these new truths to follow: 

  

  

### Generate Qualified Leads

sign-up /show up = interest + trust in your expertise

warm leads, primed for deeper engagement = to know so they can do better

[intent signals]

[PA/SA] - deciding factor; open the door they buy because you gave them the X

[PA/SU] - standout they seek who show up to serve before offers to solve, front runner b/c of the X

  

  

### Build Your Authority

repeats = known for temp goes up

deliver the quick wins that move them forward every time = easy to deliver sequels

more sequel tickets sold = you become the 'legacy' , the GOAT, the Neo: Star Wars anyone?

compound effect

go-to expert in your field, gain trust that lasts beyond the event.

  

  

### [Powerful] ICP Intel / Engagement Amplification

attendees are decision-makers, influencers, and thought leaders. They arrive primed to connect with valuable content

[want the discussion, they show up to you to have it with you because they trust you to have the deeper convos that matter, they spread your street cred which amplifies your message]

[industry intel, when you're the go-to who they spill to, you can be the one to effect real world change to take a message and turn it into a movement if you listen and you want to]

  

* * *

## Your Step-by-Step Event Success Guide

Need me to say it again, I will.

Experience is the means you can control. Results are the ends you can't. Well, not exactly.

To stand the best chance of hitting the specific, measurable end goals you seek, you've got to rely on others to do what you want them to do.

Things like, make a purchase, book a call, promote your brand that you're most likely to ask for when you close your event are just that, asks.

Your expected results are, at best, projections based on previous performance.

Planning and hosting a successful LinkedIn event takes both strategy and precision. Here’s how to create an experience your audience will remember:

### 1. Define Clear Objectives

What’s the purpose of your event? Whether it’s lead generation, relationship-building, or establishing brand authority, define your goals clearly. This will guide your content, messaging, and promotional efforts.

**Pro Tip:** Focus on delivering value to your audience. A self-serving agenda is easy to spot and will turn attendees off.

### 2. Choose a Topic That Resonates

Your topic is the bait that attracts your audience. Make it specific, actionable, and relevant to their needs. Solve a pressing problem or share insights that your audience craves.

For example: _“From Profile to Profit: Turning LinkedIn Connections into Clients.”_

* * *

### 3. Promote Like a Pro

A successful event doesn’t happen without a strong promotional strategy. Here’s how to ensure your audience shows up:

*   **Direct Invites:** Send personalized invitations to key connections.
    
*   **Engaging Content:** Share teaser posts, countdowns, and updates.
    
*   **LinkedIn Ads:** Expand your reach with targeted advertising.
    
*   **Event Hashtags:** Use a unique hashtag to boost visibility.
    

The more intentional your promotion, the better your turnout will be.

* * *

### 4. Deliver an Engaging Experience

When the event starts, make it unforgettable. Here’s how to captivate your audience:

*   **Interactive Tools:** Incorporate polls, Q&A, or live chat for real-time interaction.
    
*   **Personalized Touches:** Acknowledge attendees by name and respond to their questions.
    
*   **Valuable Resources:** Share checklists, templates, or other tools that attendees can use immediately.
    

Dynamic and interactive events ensure your audience stays engaged from start to finish.

* * *

### 5. Follow Up With Precision

Your follow-up strategy is critical to maximizing the value of your event. Here’s how to do it effectively:

*   **Thank Attendees:** Send personalized thank-you messages to everyone who joined.
    
*   **Share Recordings:** Provide access to replays for those who missed it or want to revisit key points.
    
*   **Next Steps:** Include clear calls to action, like scheduling a consultation or registering for your next event.
    

A well-executed follow-up turns attendees into loyal clients.

* * *

## Maximizing Your Event’s Impact

After your event, take time to evaluate its performance:

*   How many people attended versus how many you invited?
    
*   Which parts of the event generated the most engagement?
    
*   What feedback did attendees provide, and how can you improve next time?
    

Treat every event as a stepping stone to greater success. Use the data and feedback to refine your approach and amplify your impact.

* * *

LinkedIn events and webinars aren’t just another marketing tactic—they’re a gateway to building meaningful relationships, generating leads, and solidifying your authority. Approach them with care and strategy, and you’ll unlock an unparalleled growth channel.

### Suggested Rewrite for **Build Your Authority**

Imagine this: You’re scrolling through LinkedIn and a webinar invitation pops up that seems tailor-made for your challenges. Within moments, you’re registering, eager to learn. Hosting a session that delivers actionable insights or unpacks trends specific to your industry positions you as more than a presenter—you’re the expert who understands their pain points and offers real solutions. It’s not about dazzling with perfection; it’s about connecting through authenticity. When you present with clarity and confidence, you create trust and curiosity that linger far beyond the event.

But authority isn’t built on knowledge alone—it’s what you do with it. Choose a topic that solves a pressing problem, engage your audience with tailored value, and show them why your expertise is indispensable.

Here’s how you can take the first steps to solidify your authority.

### Suggested Rewrite for Step #1: Define Clear Objectives

* * *

Before you set up your LinkedIn event, take a moment to define your objectives. Are you looking to grow your network, generate high-quality leads, or position yourself as the authority in your niche? The clearer your goals, the easier it will be to measure success and tailor your content to meet those targets.

Think of it like planning a road trip: If you don’t know your destination, how can you map your route? Without clear objectives, your event risks being a generic presentation that blends into the crowd rather than standing out as a game-changing experience.

Start by answering these questions:

*   What action do I want attendees to take after the event?
    
*   How will this event align with my long-term business goals?
    
*   What metrics will I use to measure success (e.g., sign-ups, attendance rate, conversions)?
    

Once you’ve pinpointed your objectives, they’ll guide every aspect of your event—from the promotional strategy to the content delivery.

* * *

### Your Step-by-Step Event Success Guide

### 1. Define Clear Objectives

Nail down what success looks like before you do anything else. Is this event about pulling in leads, deepening your network, or proving you’re the one to watch in your industry? With clear objectives, you’re not just winging it—you’re working toward results that matter.

### 2. Know Exactly Who You’re Talking To

Let’s face it, not everyone on LinkedIn is your ideal fit, and that’s okay. Get specific. Who needs to be in the room? What’s keeping them up at night? When you know your audience like the back of your hand, you can deliver content that feels like it was made just for them.

### 3. Create Content They Can’t Ignore

Your event content isn’t just filler—it’s the hook, the story, and the “wow, I needed that” moment all rolled into one. Give them practical takeaways, surprising insights, and maybe even a little “aha!” moment. This is your chance to make them walk away thinking, “I’ve got to work with this person.”

### 4. Hype It Like a Pro

No one’s showing up to a party they didn’t know about. Post about your event on LinkedIn, hit up your email list, and send personal invites to people who’ll get the most out of it. Use teasers, sneak peeks, and a countdown to build FOMO. If it feels like a must-attend, it will be.

### 5. Make the Event an Experience

You’ve got their attention—now keep it. Encourage questions, real-time reactions, and lively discussions. Use polls, breakout rooms, or even quick challenges to keep the energy high. The more interactive it feels, the more they’ll remember it—and you.

### 6. Close the Loop Like a Boss

The event isn’t over when the session ends. Follow up with personalized messages, a recap, or bonus content they weren’t expecting. Keep the conversation going. This is where relationships solidify, and opportunities multiply.

### Your Step-by-Step Event Success Guide

### 2. Pinpoint Your Target Audience

### 3. Craft Compelling Event Content

### 4. Promote Strategically

Promotion isn’t just about getting the word out—it’s about creating anticipation. Use LinkedIn posts, personal messages, and your email list to showcase what’s in it for them. Teasers, countdowns, and sneak peeks build the kind of buzz that fills virtual seats fast.

### 5. Foster Real-Time Engagement

Bring energy to the event. Create space for questions, run live polls, and spark discussions. The more your audience feels involved, the more memorable the experience becomes. Engagement isn’t just fun—it’s how trust gets built.

### 6. Follow-Up with Precision

What you do after the event is just as important as the event itself. Send personal thank-you messages, share highlights, and provide any promised resources. Keep the conversation alive to turn interest into real opportunities.
